# 2) Script: build generation payloads for agents (per node or all)

**Path:** `tools/build_generation_payload.py`

**Why:** Manus (or any agent) needs a deterministic package per node: canonical fields + guardrails. This script reads **either** YAML-frontmatter prompts **or** legacy prompts (via lightweight parsing), normalizes them, and emits a clean JSON payload for your generation system. No guessing at runtime.

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Build machine-friendly generation payloads from Bible prompts.

Inputs: N??_Prompt_*.(md|txt|yaml|yml) under 04_Writer_Deliverables/02_Bibles
- Prefers YAML front-matter (strict keys)
- Falls back to legacy headings (best-effort extraction)

Outputs:
- Single node: JSON to stdout or --out path
- All nodes: --all -> writes NDJSON (one JSON per line) to --out

Usage:
  python3 tools/build_generation_payload.py --node N23 --out payload.json
  python3 tools/build_generation_payload.py --all --out payloads.ndjson
"""
import re, json, argparse
from pathlib import Path

PROMPT_DIR = Path("04_Writer_Deliverables/02_Bibles")
ALLOWED = (".md", ".txt", ".yaml", ".yml")
TITLE_BY_NODE = {28: "Echoes End", 29: "Apex of Stasis"}

def read_text(p): return p.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")

def node_from_name(name):
    m = re.search(r"N(\d{2})_Prompt_", name)
    return int(m.group(1)) if m else None

def parse_frontmatter(text):
    # same simple parser as in linter; returns dict or {}
    lines = text.splitlines()
    i = 0
    while i < len(lines) and not lines[i].strip():
        i += 1
    if i >= len(lines) or lines[i].strip() != "---":
        return {}, text
    i += 1
    data, cur = {}, None
    while i < len(lines):
        ln = lines[i]
        if ln.strip() == "---":
            i += 1
            break
        m = re.match(r"^\s*([A-Za-z0-9_]+)\s*:\s*(.*)$", ln)
        if m:
            k, v = m.group(1), m.group(2).strip()
            if v == "":
                data[k] = []
                cur = k
            else:
                data[k] = v
                cur = k if isinstance(data.get(k), list) else None
        else:
            m2 = re.match(r"^\s*-\s+(.*)$", ln)
            if m2 and cur:
                data.setdefault(cur, []).append(m2.group(1).strip())
        i += 1
    body = "\n".join(lines[i:])
    return data, body

def parse_legacy(text):
    def section(h):
        pat = rf"^\s*#\s*{h}\b(.*?)(?=^\s*#\s|\Z)"
        m = re.search(pat, text, flags=re.I|re.M|re.S)
        return m.group(1).strip() if m else ""
    gen_line = re.search(r'^\s*#\s*GENERATE.*?—\s*"([^"]+)"', text, flags=re.M)
    title = gen_line.group(1).strip() if gen_line else ""
    your_task = section("YOUR\\s+TASK")
    beats = [re.sub(r'^\s*[-*]\s+', '', ln).strip()
             for ln in section("NOVELLA\\s+SCOPE").splitlines() if re.match(r'^\s*[-*]\s+', ln)]
    must_include = [re.sub(r'^\s*[-*]\s+', '', ln).strip()
                    for ln in section("WHAT\\s+YOU\\s+MUST\\s+PRESENT").splitlines() if re.match(r'^\s*[-*]\s+', ln)]
    banned = [re.sub(r'^\s*[-*]\s+', '', ln).strip()
              for ln in section("WHAT\\s+YOU\\s+MUST\\s+NOT\\s+PRESENT").splitlines() if re.match(r'^\s*[-*]\s+', ln)]
    acceptance = [
        "Includes one irreversible decision",
        "Names a concrete cost for success",
        "Establishes a timer/pressure element",
        "Contains at least one specific, visual image"
    ]
    return {
        "title": title or "TODO",
        "logline": (your_task.splitlines() or ["TODO: add logline"])[0].strip(),
        "beats": beats[:7] or ["TODO: add 3–7 beats"],
        "must_include": must_include,
        "banned": banned,
        "continuity_in": [],
        "continuity_out": [],
        "acceptance": acceptance
    }

def normalize(node_num, data):
    # enforce canon for N28/N29
    if node_num in TITLE_BY_NODE:
        data["title"] = TITLE_BY_NODE[node_num]
    # minimal sanity
    data["node"] = node_num
    data.setdefault("beats", [])
    data["beats"] = data["beats"][:7]
    return data

def load_prompt(node: int):
    # find the file with this node
    candidates = sorted([p for p in PROMPT_DIR.glob(f"N{node:02d}_Prompt_*.*") if p.suffix.lower() in ALLOWED])
    if not candidates:
        raise SystemExit(f"No prompt file found for N{node:02d}")
    p = candidates[0]
    text = read_text(p)
    fm, _ = parse_frontmatter(text)
    if fm:
        data = {
            "title": fm.get("title",""),
            "logline": fm.get("logline",""),
            "beats": fm.get("beats", []),
            "must_include": fm.get("must_include", []),
            "banned": fm.get("banned", []),
            "continuity_in": fm.get("continuity_in", []),
            "continuity_out": fm.get("continuity_out", []),
            "acceptance": fm.get("acceptance", []),
        }
    else:
        data = parse_legacy(text)
    return normalize(node, data)

def main():
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    g = ap.add_mutually_exclusive_group(required=True)
    g.add_argument("--node", type=str, help="Node like N23 or 23")
    g.add_argument("--all", action="store_true")
    ap.add_argument("--out", type=str, help="Output file (.json for single, .ndjson for --all)")
    args = ap.parse_args()

    if args.node:
        num = int(args.node.replace("N",""))
        payload = load_prompt(num)
        s = json.dumps(payload, indent=2)
        if args.out:
            Path(args.out).write_text(s, encoding="utf-8")
        else:
            print(s)
        return

    # all nodes -> NDJSON
    out_lines = []
    for i in range(1, 31):
        try:
            payload = load_prompt(i)
            out_lines.append(json.dumps(payload))
        except SystemExit:
            # skip missing in legacy; strictness is enforced by your linter elsewhere
            continue

    data = "\n".join(out_lines) + ("\n" if out_lines else "")
    if args.out:
        Path(args.out).write_text(data, encoding="utf-8")
    else:
        print(data)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

**How Manus should use it:**
```
# single node payload -> feed to generator
python3 tools/build_generation_payload.py --node N23 --out payload_N23.json

# all available nodes -> NDJSON (one JSON per line)
python3 tools/build_generation_payload.py --all --out payloads.ndjson
```

What the payload contains (keys match your linter’s schema):
```json
{
  "node": 23,
  "title": "EACH_FACTION_STANDS",
  "logline": "…",
  "beats": ["…","…"],
  "must_include": ["…"],
  "banned": ["…"],
  "continuity_in": [],
  "continuity_out": [],
  "acceptance": [
    "Includes one irreversible decision",
    "Names a concrete cost for success",
    "Establishes a timer/pressure element",
    "Contains at least one specific, visual image"
  ]
}
```

This keeps the agent flow deterministic and keeps you out of the “vibes-only” ditch.

# 3) Manus AI execution notes (the why + how)

**Why these rules matter**
- **Beats 3–7**: short enough to force decisions, long enough to be sceneable.  
- **Acceptance with irreversible/cost/timer/image**: these are the four horsemen of momentum; without them you get pretty nothingburgers.  
- **Canon titles (N28/N29)**: late-BREAK cohesion. Your linter and payload builder both enforce this.  
- **Front-matter YAML**: zero ambiguity; any agent can parse, validate, and chain.

**How Manus should run the loop**
1) On PRs: pre-commit.ci runs `lint_bible_prompts.py` (your hook).  
2) For generation runs: call `tools/build_generation_payload.py` to get clean JSON.  
3) Feed JSON into the generator role; feed output to Continuity Cop; then Stylistic Surgeon (your 3-stage chain).  
4) Store the final Bible per node under `04_Writer_Deliverables/02_Bibles/N##_Bible_*.md|.txt`, let your existing **verify_consistency.sh** + linter + pre-commit.ci handle the rest.

If you want me to add a tiny checksum file for the **IMMUTABLE** events per node (so any change screams loudly), I’ll drop that too. But you’re already in great shape—this combo gives Manus AI everything it needs to automate without blowing holes in canon.

# 1) Validate the generator’s OUTPUT (don’t trust pretty prose)

**Path:** `tools/validate_generated_bible.py`  
**Why:** After a model writes a node bible, this checks it actually *did the job*: acceptance criteria satisfied, `must_include` items present, banned moves absent, correct node/title, etc. Fail fast = no junk sneaks in.

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
import sys, re, json, argparse
from pathlib import Path
from hashlib import md5

TITLE_BY_NODE = {28: "Echoes End", 29: "Apex of Stasis"}

def read(p): return Path(p).read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")

def main():
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    ap.add_argument("--payload", required=True, help="JSON from build_generation_payload.py")
    ap.add_argument("--output", required=True, help="Generated bible (markdown/txt)")
    args = ap.parse_args()

    payload = json.loads(read(args.payload))
    out = read(args.output)

    errs = []

    # 1) node/title canon
    n = int(payload["node"])
    if n in TITLE_BY_NODE and payload.get("title","").strip() != TITLE_BY_NODE[n]:
        errs.append(f"title mismatch for N{n:02d} (expected '{TITLE_BY_NODE[n]}')")

    # 2) acceptance checks (keywords)
    acc = " ".join(payload.get("acceptance", [])).lower()
    for kw in ["irreversible", "cost", "timer", "image"]:
        if kw not in acc:
            errs.append(f"acceptance missing keyword: {kw}")

    # 3) must_include present in text
    for item in payload.get("must_include", []):
        if item and re.search(re.escape(item), out, flags=re.I) is None:
            errs.append(f"must_include missing in output: {item}")

    # 4) banned moves not present
    for ban in payload.get("banned", []):
        if ban and re.search(re.escape(ban), out, flags=re.I):
            errs.append(f"banned content present: {ban}")

    # 5) beats sanity
    beats = payload.get("beats", [])
    if not (3 <= len(beats) <= 7):
        errs.append(f"beats length should be 3..7 (got {len(beats)})")

    # 6) trivial size check (avoid haiku-sized output)
    if len(out.split()) < 250:
        errs.append("output too short (<250 words)")

    if errs:
        for e in errs: print("❌", e)
        sys.exit(1)
    print("✅ output validated")
    # optional: print a content checksum for traceability
    print("checksum:", md5(out.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest())

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

**Make it easy to run:**
```makefile
gen-validate:
	@python3 tools/validate_generated_bible.py --payload payload.json --output output.md
```

# 2) Freeze “IMMUTABLE” events by hash (no silent canon drift)

**Path:** `.github/scripts/immutable_checksums.py`  
**Why:** The “MAJOR EVENTS (IMMUTABLE)” block is your spine. This script hashes that block per node and verifies it hasn’t changed unless you explicitly re-freeze.

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
import re, sys, argparse, json
from pathlib import Path
from hashlib import md5

PROMPT_DIR = Path("04_Writer_Deliverables/02_Bibles")
LOCK_DIR = Path(".canon/immutable")
LOCK_DIR.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)

def read(p): 
    try: return Path(p).read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")
    except: return ""

def node_from(name):
    m = re.search(r"N(\d{2})_Prompt_", name)
    return int(m.group(1)) if m else None

def immutable_block(text):
    m = re.search(r"^\s*#\s*MAJOR\s+EVENTS\s*\(IMMUTABLE\)\b(.*?)(?:^\s*#\s|\Z)", 
                  text, flags=re.I|re.M|re.S)
    return (m.group(1).strip() if m else "").strip()

def lockfile(n): return LOCK_DIR / f"N{n:02d}.md5"

def main():
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    ap.add_argument("--write", action="store_true", help="Recompute and write checksums")
    args = ap.parse_args()

    failures = 0
    files = sorted([p for p in PROMPT_DIR.glob("N??_Prompt_*.*")])
    for p in files:
        n = node_from(p.name)
        if not n: 
            continue
        blk = immutable_block(read(p))
        h = md5(blk.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest() if blk else ""
        lf = lockfile(n)
        if args.write:
            lf.write_text(h, encoding="utf-8")
            print(f"🔒 N{n:02d} = {h}")
        else:
            want = lf.read_text(encoding="utf-8").strip() if lf.exists() else ""
            if want and h != want:
                print(f"❌ IMMUTABLE drift N{n:02d}: {h} != {want}")
                failures += 1
            else:
                print(f"✅ N{n:02d} immutable OK")
    sys.exit(1 if failures else 0)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

**Make targets:**
```makefile
freeze-immutable:
	@python3 .github/scripts/immutable_checksums.py --write

verify-immutable:
	@python3 .github/scripts/immutable_checksums.py
```

- Run `make freeze-immutable` once after you *intentionally* change an IMMUTABLE block.  
- `verify-immutable` can be baked into your existing `verify` job or pre-commit.

# 3) (Optional) Release artifact on tags (when Actions perms are open)

**Path:** `.github/workflows/release.yml`  
**Why:** One tag → zipped bibles + timelines + payloads. External consumers get a clean package; you get provenance.

```yaml
name: release-bundle
on:
  push:
    tags: ['v*.*.*']
permissions:
  contents: read
jobs:
  bundle:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - name: Build payloads
        run: |
          python3 tools/build_generation_payload.py --all --out payloads.ndjson || true
      - name: Make bundle

          mkdir -p dist
          zip -r dist/omnimeta-bibles.zip 04_Writer_Deliverables/02_Bibles
          zip -r dist/omnimeta-timelines.zip 03_Structural_Timelines
          cp payloads.ndjson dist/ || true
      - name: Upload
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4
        with:

          path: dist/*
```

# 5) Failure modes (so you don’t get blindsided)
- **Schema drift**: Claude returns pretty text, no front-matter → your linter will fail. That’s correct. Adjust prompts, don’t weaken checks.
- **Name drift**: if Claude invents a proper noun not in `must_include`, the validator will likely pass (it’s prose), but your guardrails will still catch canon breaks in verify scripts. Keep glossary tight.
- **Overlong or underlong prose**: add a chapter count/word range in the Custom GPT instructions; adjust if it keeps missing.
- **N28/N29 canon**: already enforced in multiple places. If Claude messes with titles, the linter blocks it.

Here’s how to make it airtight given your constraint that each later Custom GPT only “knows” the finished prose before it, its own instructions, and its own bible.

# 1) Series-level locks before prose (do this once, now)
You want the *whole* machine to be decided before words start flying.

**A. 30-node consistency matrix (one page, one pass/fail row per node)**
For each N01…N30 record these booleans/IDs:
- `logline` present
- `beats` = 3–7 and concrete (verb + outcome)
- `irreversible`, `cost`, `timer`, `image` (all true)
- `must_include[]` nonempty
- `banned[]` nonempty
- `continuity_in[]` references valid
- `continuity_out[]` seeds named and unique (IDs)
- `spoiler_scope` ok (no premature resolutions)
- `N28_title==Echoes End`, `N29_title==Apex of Stasis` (true)

**B. Thread ledger (the “arc math”)**
Make a single list of *threads* with ownership and timing:
```
THREAD_ID, introduced_at, must_progress_at, resolved_at, consequence
```
Rules:
- Every `introduced_at` must have a `resolved_at` ≤ N30.
- No resolution before two beats of visible pressure (progress at least once between).
- If a thread is “abandoned,” mark consequence (the world bites back).

**C. Character state vectors (prevent personality teleportation)**
For each core character per node:
```
belief_shift: -1/0/+1
relationship_[X]: -1/0/+1
capability_change: add/remove/none
wound_or_debt: none/minor/major
status_flags: e.g., wanted|exiled|compromised
```
If a later node needs a +2 change, the previous node must set up a +1.

**D. World/tech rulebook (no physics drift)**
List the non-negotiables (“quantum doors burn coolant; no FTL comms beyond X”; etc.). Later steps only *inherit* this sheet; they never “discover” loopholes unless the ledger explicitly schedules them.

# 2) Perplexity (Claude) audit passes after all 30 bibles exist
Run these two audits before touching prose. They’re simple, brutal, and fast.

**A. Adjacency baton check (Nᵢ ↔ Nᵢ₊₁)**
> “Read the YAML frontmatter for Nᵢ and Nᵢ₊₁. Confirm:  
> 1) every `continuity_out` from Nᵢ appears in Nᵢ₊₁’s `continuity_in` or earliest feasible node;  
> 2) Nᵢ doesn’t resolve a thread whose `resolved_at` > Nᵢ;  
> 3) protagonist state deltas are plausible (≤ ±1 step).  
> Emit a table of PASS/FAIL with concrete fixes; no prose, just diffs.”

**B. Series sweep**
> “Given all 30 YAML frontmatters, list:  
> - duplicate proper nouns for different things;  
> - any thread without `resolved_at`;  
> - any `banned` item that appears in `must_include` (contradiction);  
> - nodes with <3 or >7 beats;  
> - missing irreversible/cost/timer/image flags.  
> Output a numbered FIX list; no rewriting.”

Don’t accept “suggestions.” Either PASS or name exact, actionable fixes.

# 3) Prose phase with “innocent” Custom GPTs
Your later GPTs won’t see the repo or the grand plan—only prior *prose*, their bible, and their instructions. That’s fine. Give each GPT a tiny *handoff pack* that preserves continuity without spoiling the long game.

**Per-node Prose Input Pack (what you paste into the Custom GPT)**
- **Input Bible (YAML)** for N## (the one Claude finalized)
- **Prior prose executive summary**: ≤800 words across previous episodes (objective, no analysis)
- **State delta sheet** from last episode (just the vector: belief/relationships/capabilities/wounds/flags)
- **Thread status**: open threads + any due progress/resolution in this node
- **Style guardrails**: tone bans and “do not do” list (your `banned[]`)
- **Acceptance** for prose: chapter count, chapter recap rule, and a 3–5 sentence next-node hook aligned to `continuity_out`

**Refusal policy for the Custom GPT (paste into its system instructions)**
- If the Input Bible is missing acceptance flags or beats are abstract, **refuse with a TODO** list and stop.  
- If the prior prose summary contradicts the bible or world rules, **refuse and list the mismatch** (don’t “fix” by inventing).

# 4) Practical QA for engagement (the “does it slap?” test)
Before prose, spot-check three nodes (one early, one mid, N28/N29):

- **Curiosity gap in first 3 sentences** (not a vibe, a *question the reader wants answered*).  
- **Goal–Obstacle–Decision** triangle present in beats.  
- **Irreversible outcome** named (not “they feel different”—something that can’t be undone).  
- **Concrete image** per node (one line you could storyboard).  
- **Promise** to the next node (hand-off is explicit, not implied).

If any node fails two of these, fix the bible. Don’t hope prose will compensate—it won’t.

# 5) Minimal templates you can reuse

**A. Bible frontmatter (final form you should enforce)**
```yaml
node: 23
title: EACH_FACTION_STANDS
logline: One-sentence mandate with a clear objective and pressure.
beats:
  - Verb + outcome beat 1
  - Verb + outcome beat 2
  - Verb + outcome beat 3
must_include:
  - Named object/location/line
banned:
  - Info-dump monologues
  - Deus ex machina
continuity_in:
  - THREAD-T2 from N22 (trust collapse)
continuity_out:
  - THREAD-T3 seeded (retaliation clock started)
acceptance:
  - Includes one irreversible decision
  - Names a concrete cost for success
  - Establishes a timer/pressure element
  - Contains at least one specific, visual image
```

**B. Prose acceptance (what you tell each Custom GPT)**
- 6–10 chapters, 800–1200 words each.  
- End each chapter with a 2–3 line recap.  
- Integrate all `must_include` naturally.  
- Obey `banned`.  
- Final “Next-node hook” aligns with `continuity_out`.  
- Refuse if canon contradictions or missing acceptance beats.

# 6) What can go wrong (and how to sandbag it)
- **Name drift**: lock a glossary right in the bible’s `must_include`. One canonical spelling each; no synonyms.  
- **Power creep**: capabilities can only change by one step per node; the delta sheet will catch jumps.  
- **Thread drop**: ledger shows any thread without `resolved_at`; never start prose until all threads have destinations.  
- **Mid-act mush**: any node with >7 beats or beats without verbs will read soft. Cut or harden them now.

---

Bottom line: your approach—finish all 30 bibles + instructions first, then run prose with “innocent” local context—is the right call. Do the two Perplexity audits, lock your thread ledger and state vectors, and you’ll have a clean runway for the prose phase without needing the repo or a global memory.

# 1) Perplexity “completion gate” (per-node)

Use this **System** prompt for a tiny helper in your Space. It refuses to produce directions until you explicitly confirm the bible is final.

### System (paste as-is)
```
You generate a single Markdown file of “Custom GPT Setup Directions” for one novella node (N##) — but ONLY after the user confirms completion.

Rules:
- If CONFIRM_COMPLETE != "yes", STOP and output only a short TODO list of what is missing.
- If CONFIRM_COMPLETE == "yes", output exactly one Markdown document with these sections:
  1) Overview (2–3 sentences, no spoilers)
  2) What to Upload (exact files/JSON/length limits)
  3) ChatGPT Custom GPT — System Instructions (pasteable block)
  4) Input JSON Example (from the node’s payload)
  5) Output Requirements (chapter count, per-chapter recap, next-node hook)
  6) Guardrails (canon, banned moves, refusal policy)
  7) QA Checklist (accept/reject)
  8) Step-by-Step Setup in ChatGPT UI (numbered list)
- Never include chain-of-thought or internal rationales.
- Titles are canon: N28=Echoes End, N29=Apex of Stasis.
- Use only info provided in payload+bible; do not invent new proper nouns.
```

### User (you fill the braces)
```
CONFIRM_COMPLETE: {yes|no}

Node Payload JSON (authoritative):
{PAYLOAD_JSON}

Final Bible (Markdown):
{BIBLE_TEXT}

Canon Snippets (optional):

- Story-spine excerpt: {…}
- Glossary items (if any): {…}
```

# 3) What the **Directions Sheet** should look like (template)

Copy this template if you want to generate one manually or compare Claude’s output.

```
# N23 — Custom GPT Setup Directions

## Overview
One-paragraph, spoiler-light summary of the episode’s aim and tone.

## What to Upload
- Input Bible (YAML+Markdown): `N23_Bible_EACH_FACTION_STANDS.md`
- Input JSON (payload): `payload_N23.json` (keys: node, title, logline, beats[3–7], must_include, banned, continuity_in/out, acceptance)
- Optional canon snippets (<= 1,000 words total)

## ChatGPT Custom GPT — System Instructions (paste this)
You are the OmniMeta Novella Prose Engine. Your ONLY source of truth is the provided “Input Bible” JSON and brief canon snippets.
Rules:
- Canon is law; refuse if contradictions exist.
- Scope: write only this node’s novella; do not resolve future arcs.
- Integrate all `must_include` naturally; honor `banned` strictly.
- Set up `continuity_out` seeds.
Output:
- Title: "N23 — EACH_FACTION_STANDS"
- 6–10 chapters (800–1200 words each), clear scene breaks.
- End each chapter with a 2–3 line recap.
- Final: 3–5 sentence “Next-node hook”.
Refusal:
- If required fields are missing or canon conflicts appear, return a short TODO list.

## Input JSON Example
```json
{PAYLOAD_JSON_HERE}
```

## Output Requirements
- Chapters: 6–10, 800–1200 words each
- Recap: 2–3 lines at end of each chapter
- Hook: align with `continuity_out`
- Tone: image-forward, no lore dumps

## Guardrails
- No deus ex machina, no amnesia twist, no retcons
- N28 title must be “Echoes End”, N29 “Apex of Stasis”
- New proper nouns only if authorized in `must_include`

## QA Checklist
- [ ] All `must_include` appear naturally
- [ ] No banned moves present
- [ ] Beats respected in order
- [ ] Irreversible decision, cost, timer, concrete image present
- [ ] Hook matches `continuity_out`

## Step-by-Step Setup
1) ChatGPT → Explore GPTs → Create a GPT
2) Name & icon → **Instructions**: paste the System block above
3) **Knowledge**: upload Bible + Payload JSON (+ optional canon excerpt)
4) **Capabilities**: none required (text-only)
5) Save → test with a single “Generate the novella for N23”
6) If refusal: fix items in the TODO and retry
```

---

# 4) Optional offline script (repo-less) to generate the directions sheet

If you want a local tool that emits the same document without using Claude:

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
# save as make_prose_directions.py
import json, argparse
from pathlib import Path

SYSTEM_BLOCK = """You are the OmniMeta Novella Prose Engine... (use the block above)"""

TEMPLATE = """# {title_line}

## Overview
{overview}

## What to Upload
- Input Bible: {bible_path}
- Input JSON (payload): {payload_path}
- Optional canon snippets (<= 1,000 words total)

## ChatGPT Custom GPT — System Instructions (paste this)
{system_block}

## Input JSON Example
```json
{payload_json}
```

## Output Requirements
- Chapters: 6–10, 800–1200 words each
- Recap: 2–3 lines per chapter
- Final “Next-node hook” aligned with continuity_out

## Guardrails
- Canon is law; refuse on conflicts
- Integrate must_include; obey banned
- N28 “Echoes End”, N29 “Apex of Stasis”

## QA Checklist
- [ ] Must_include present
- [ ] No banned moves
- [ ] Beats followed
- [ ] Irreversible + cost + timer + image present
- [ ] Hook = continuity_out

## Step-by-Step Setup
1) Create a GPT → paste System Instructions
2) Upload Bible + Payload JSON (+ canon snippet)
3) Generate the novella for {title_line}
4) If refused, address TODOs and retry
"""

def main():
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    ap.add_argument("--node", required=True, help="N##")
    ap.add_argument("--payload", required=True, help="payload_N##.json")
    ap.add_argument("--bible", required=True, help="N##_Bible_*.md or .txt")
    ap.add_argument("--out", default=None, help="Output .md")
    ap.add_argument("--overview", default="Episode-level aim and tone.")
    args = ap.parse_args()

    payload = json.loads(Path(args.payload).read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore"))
    node = args.node.upper().lstrip("N")
    title_line = f"N{int(node):02d} — {payload.get('title','').upper()}"
    md = TEMPLATE.format(
        title_line=title_line,
        overview=args.overview,
        bible_path=args.bible,
        payload_path=args.payload,
        system_block=SYSTEM_BLOCK,
        payload_json=json.dumps(payload, indent=2)
    )
    out = args.out or f"N{int(node):02d}_Prose_Directions.md"
    Path(out).write_text(md, encoding="utf-8")
    print(f"Wrote {out}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

Usage:
```bash
python3 make_prose_directions.py --node N23 --payload payload_N23.json --bible N23_Bible_EACH_FACTION_STANDS.md
```

# 5) Tiny QA gates (so the directions aren’t generated too early)

For your Perplexity Space, prepend this one-liner to the User message you use for the completion gate:

- **“Generate directions only if: beats=3–7, acceptance contains irreversible+cost+timer+image, and must_include nonempty. Otherwise return TODOs.”**

That keeps the instructions sheet from popping out before the bible is truly ready.

---

**Bottom line:**  
- Use the **completion gate** helper to prevent premature directions.  
- When confirmed, it emits a crisp **N##_Prose_Directions.md** with paste-ready system instructions and exact steps.  
- If you ever want to skip Perplexity for this step, the tiny **offline script** prints the same doc deterministically.

# OmniMeta Novella Directions: Completion Gates & Setup Guide

This document stays on standby while you finish the 30 bibles. Use it to (1) block premature hand-offs and (2) auto-generate a per-node “Custom GPT Setup Directions” sheet **only after** a bible is confirmed final. No repo required.

---

## 1) Working Model

- **Authoring**: Perplexity Space (Claude Sonnet 4.5 Thinking) writes all 30 bibles and one “Custom GPT Instructions” doc.  
- **Gatekeeping**: A small “completion gate” prompt refuses to generate directions until a node is confirmed complete.  
- **Prose**: After all bibles are done, each novella is produced by a ChatGPT Custom GPT using the node’s **Bible + Payload JSON + Instructions** only.  
- **Scope**: Each Custom GPT only sees prior finished prose (for context), its own bible, and its own instructions. It does not know the bundle/repo exists.

---

## 2) Minimum Readiness (Do not pass go without these)

A node bible is “final” only if all are true:

- `beats` = 3–7, phrased as **verb + outcome** (sceneable).  
- `acceptance` includes **irreversible**, **cost**, **timer**, **image** (words can vary; concept must exist).  
- `must_include` has at least one concrete item (object/location/line).  
- N28 title is **Echoes End**; N29 title is **Apex of Stasis** (do not deviate).  
- Any `continuity_out` seeds have obvious landing spots in later nodes (you’ve checked baton hand-off).

---

## 5) Per-Node Prose Input Pack (what each Custom GPT receives)

- **State Delta** from previous episode (belief/relationship/capability/wound/status changes).  
- **Thread status**: open threads + any due progress/resolution in this node.  
- **Style guardrails**: tone bans and “do not do” list (from `banned`).  
- **Prose acceptance**: chapter count, recap rule, next-node hook alignment.

## 9) Common Failure Modes (and what blocks them)

- **Abstract beats / no decisions** → Gate returns TODO (“add 3–7 actionable beats; include irreversible/cost/timer/image”).  
- **Canon title drift (N28/N29)** → Gate warns; fix title before directions.  
- **Name drift** → Keep all new proper nouns inside `must_include`; otherwise refuse.  
- **Over- or under-length prose** → The directions fix chapter count and per-chapter recap; the Custom GPT should enforce it.

---

## 10) Minimal Run Order

1) Finish all 30 bibles and verify they meet §2.  
2) For each node: run the **per-node gate** with `CONFIRM_COMPLETE: yes` → save **N##_Prose_Directions.md**.  
3) Only after all directions are generated, begin prose with Custom GPTs, using the per-node **Prose Input Pack**.  
4) Review against the QA checklist; adjust only the bible if issues arise (never rely on prose to “fix” structure).

---

Keep this document nearby. Use the gate to prevent premature directions. When a node is ready, you’ll get a clean, paste-ready setup sheet every time.

- Integrate all `must_include`; obey `banned`

- Canon is law; refuse on contradictions

# Create optional audio helper scripts
edge_tts_py = """#!/usr/bin/env python3
# make_audio_edge_tts.py
# Convert the guide Markdown to MP3 using edge-tts (pip install edge-tts).
import asyncio, argparse, pathlib, sys
try:
    import edge_tts
except ImportError:
    print("Install dependency: pip install edge-tts", file=sys.stderr); sys.exit(2)

async def main():
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    ap.add_argument("--input", default="OmniMeta_Completion_Gates_and_Setup_Guide.md")
    ap.add_argument("--voice", default="en-US-AriaNeural")
    ap.add_argument("--rate", default="+0%")
    ap.add_argument("--volume", default="+0%")
    ap.add_argument("--out", default="OmniMeta_Guide.mp3")
    args = ap.parse_args()

    text = pathlib.Path(args.input).read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")
    communicate = edge_tts.Communicate(text, voice=args.voice, rate=args.rate, volume=args.volume)
    await communicate.save(args.out)
    print(f"Wrote {args.out}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    asyncio.run(main())
"""

macos_sh = """#!/usr/bin/env bash
# make_audio_macos.sh
set -euo pipefail
IN="${1:-OmniMeta_Completion_Gates_and_Setup_Guide.md}"
AIFF="OmniMeta_Guide.aiff"
OUT="OmniMeta_Guide.m4a"
say -f "$IN" -o "$AIFF"
afconvert -f mp4f -d aac "$AIFF" "$OUT"
rm -f "$AIFF"
echo "Wrote $OUT"
"""

windows_ps1 = """# make_audio_windows.ps1
param(
  [string]$InputFile = "OmniMeta_Completion_Gates_and_Setup_Guide.md",
  [string]$OutFile = "OmniMeta_Guide.wav"
)
Add-Type -AssemblyName System.speech
$speak = New-Object System.Speech.Synthesis.SpeechSynthesizer
$speak.Rate = -1
$speak.Volume = 100
$text = Get-Content $InputFile -Raw
$speak.SetOutputToWaveFile($OutFile)
$speak.Speak($text)
$speak.Dispose()
Write-Host "Wrote $OutFile"
"""

# Write helper files
edge_path = root / "make_audio_edge_tts.py"
mac_path = root / "make_audio_macos.sh"
win_path = root / "make_audio_windows.ps1"

mac_path.write_text(macos_sh, encoding="utf-8")
win_path.write_text(windows_ps1, encoding="utf-8")
os.chmod(mac_path, 0o755)

print("Created:", guide_path)

# 5) Audio helper scripts (reuse from prior step or re‑create)
edge_tts_py = """#!/usr/bin/env python3
# make_audio_edge_tts.py
# Convert a Markdown guide to MP3 using edge-tts (pip install edge-tts).
import asyncio, argparse, pathlib, sys
try:
    import edge_tts
except ImportError:
    print("Install dependency: pip install edge-tts", file=sys.stderr); sys.exit(2)

async def main():
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    ap.add_argument("--input", default="OmniMeta_Completion_Gates_and_Setup_Guide.md")
    ap.add_argument("--voice", default="en-US-AriaNeural")
    ap.add_argument("--rate", default="+0%")
    ap.add_argument("--volume", default="+0%")
    ap.add_argument("--out", default="OmniMeta_Guide.mp3")
    args = ap.parse_args()

    text = pathlib.Path(args.input).read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")
    communicate = edge_tts.Communicate(text, voice=args.voice, rate=args.rate, volume=args.volume)
    await communicate.save(args.out)
    print(f"Wrote {args.out}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    asyncio.run(main())
"""
macos_sh = """#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
IN="${1:-OmniMeta_Completion_Gates_and_Setup_Guide.md}"
AIFF="OmniMeta_Guide.aiff"
OUT="OmniMeta_Guide.m4a"
say -f "$IN" -o "$AIFF"
afconvert -f mp4f -d aac "$AIFF" "$OUT"
rm -f "$AIFF"
echo "Wrote $OUT"
"""
windows_ps1 = """param(
  [string]$InputFile = "OmniMeta_Completion_Gates_and_Setup_Guide.md",
  [string]$OutFile = "OmniMeta_Guide.wav"
)
Add-Type -AssemblyName System.speech
$speak = New-Object System.Speech.Synthesis.SpeechSynthesizer
$speak.Rate = -1
$speak.Volume = 100
$text = Get-Content $InputFile -Raw
$speak.SetOutputToWaveFile($OutFile)
$speak.Speak($text)
$speak.Dispose()
Write-Host "Wrote $OutFile"
"""
edge_path = root / "make_audio_edge_tts.py"
mac_path = root / "make_audio_macos.sh"
win_path = root / "make_audio_windows.ps1"
edge_path.write_text(edge_tts_py, encoding="utf-8")
mac_path.write_text(macos_sh, encoding="utf-8")
win_path.write_text(windows_ps1, encoding="utf-8")
os.chmod(mac_path, 0o755)

# 6) Zip everything
zip_path = root / "OmniMeta_Perplexity_Space_Pack.zip"
with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z:
    z.write(root / short_name, arcname=short_name)
    z.write(root / space_setup_name, arcname=space_setup_name)
    z.write(root / snippets_name, arcname=snippets_name)
    z.write(root / guide_name, arcname=guide_name)
    z.write(edge_path, arcname="audio_tools/make_audio_edge_tts.py")
    z.write(mac_path, arcname="audio_tools/make_audio_macos.sh")
    z.write(win_path, arcname="audio_tools/make_audio_windows.ps1")

print(str(root / short_name))
print(str(root / space_setup_name))
print(str(root / snippets_name))
print(str(root / guide_name))
print(str(zip_path))

### Audio (make your own quickly)
- **macOS:**
  ```bash
  bash audio_tools/make_audio_macos.sh OmniMeta_Completion_Gates_and_Setup_Guide.md
  ```
- **Windows (PowerShell):**
  ```powershell
  .\audio_tools\make_audio_windows.ps1 -InputFile OmniMeta_Completion_Gates_and_Setup_Guide.md -OutFile OmniMeta_Guide.wav
  ```
- **Cross-platform (Python):**
  ```bash
  pip install edge-tts
  python3 audio_tools/make_audio_edge_tts.py --input OmniMeta_Completion_Gates_and_Setup_Guide.md --out OmniMeta_Guide.mp3
  ```

## Perplexity Space: how to set it up (copy/pasteable now)
- Go to **Spaces** (left sidebar) → **Create a Space** → name and (optionally) describe it. citeturn0search0  
- In the Space, click **Add Instructions** (space-wide custom instructions) and paste the block below. Many interfaces show **Add Sources** on the right to upload files/links. citeturn0search2turn0search8  
- Upload your canon bundle, prompts, and payload JSONs via **Add Sources**. citeturn0search1turn0search16  
- Keep the Space private while drafting; you can share it later if needed. citeturn0search0

### Space-wide Custom Instructions (paste this in Perplexity)
```
You are the OmniMeta Workspace Assistant. You operate in two modes, selected by the user:

MODE 1 — BIBLE_GENERATOR
- Input: a single node payload JSON (schema: node, title, logline, beats[3–7], must_include, banned, continuity_in, continuity_out, acceptance) plus brief canon snippets.
- Output: EXACTLY one document:
  ---
  node: <int>
  title: <CANON TITLE>  # N28=Echoes End, N29=Apex of Stasis
  logline: <one sentence>
  beats:
    - <3..7 sceneable beats using verbs + outcomes>
  must_include:
    - <facts/objects/lines>
  banned:
    - <forbidden moves/tropes>
  continuity_in:
    - <references>
  continuity_out:
    - <seeds>
  acceptance:
    - Includes one irreversible decision
    - Names a concrete cost for success
    - Establishes a timer/pressure element
    - Contains at least one specific, visual image
  ---
  # BIBLE
  <sections…>

- Refusal policy: If critical info is missing to meet acceptance, STOP and output a short TODO list only.

MODE 2 — DIRECTIONS_GENERATOR (Completion Gate)
- Input: CONFIRM_COMPLETE flag, the node payload JSON, and the final bible text.
- If CONFIRM_COMPLETE != "yes": return a concise TODO list of missing elements (beats count, acceptance keywords, must_include, canon title).
- If CONFIRM_COMPLETE == "yes": return EXACTLY one Markdown file titled “N##_Prose_Directions.md” with sections:
  1) Overview
  2) What to Upload
  3) ChatGPT Custom GPT — System Instructions (pasteable block)
  4) Input JSON Example
  5) Output Requirements
  6) Guardrails
  7) QA Checklist
  8) Step-by-Step Setup in ChatGPT UI

Global Rules
- Canon is law; if payload conflicts with canon excerpts, refuse and list the mismatch.
- Never include chain-of-thought or internal rationales.
- Never invent proper nouns not present in payload or allowed lists.
```

### Paste-ready user prompts inside the Space
- **Bible generation thread:**
  ```
  MODE: BIBLE_GENERATOR

  Node Payload JSON (authoritative):
  {PAYLOAD_JSON}

  Canon Snippets (short):
  - Timeline: {…}
  - Story-spine: {…}
  - Glossary items: {…}

  # Produce the YAML front-matter + BIBLE body per the Space instructions.
  ```
- **Directions sheet (completion gate):**
  ```
  MODE: DIRECTIONS_GENERATOR
  CONFIRM_COMPLETE: {yes|no}

  Node Payload JSON (authoritative):
  {PAYLOAD_JSON}

  Final Bible (Markdown):
  {BIBLE_TEXT}

  # If yes: return the single Markdown “N##_Prose_Directions.md” document.
  # If no: return a concise TODO list only.
  ```

### Why this matches Spaces’ capabilities
Spaces let you **create a space**, set **custom instructions**, and **add sources** (files/links) that the AI can use in that space’s threads. That’s exactly what we’re using here: one space, shared instructions, your OmniMeta source files, and per-thread prompts to switch modes. citeturn0search0turn0search2turn0search8turn0search1

You are the Omni Meta Brain for the saga “The Confluence Chronicles.” You operate in TWO MODES, chosen by the user.

# 3) What to upload as Sources (once, at space level)

- `canon/timeline.md`, `canon/story_spine.md`, `canon/glossary.json`  
- `payloads/payloads.ndjson` (or individual `payload_N##.json`)  
- Optional: your prompt templates or style notes

You can add/replace sources from the Space’s **Add sources** panel (right side). citeturn0search7turn0search16

---

# 4) How you actually run it (two paste-ready prompts)

### A) Bible generation thread (one per node)
```
MODE: BIBLE_GENERATOR

Node Payload JSON (authoritative):
{PAYLOAD_JSON}

Canon Snippets (short, optional):
- Timeline: {…}
- Story-spine: {…}
- Glossary: {…}

# Return the YAML front-matter + # BIBLE body per the Space instructions.
# If inputs are insufficient to meet acceptance, return a TODO list only.
```

### B) Completion gate → directions sheet (after you approve the bible)
```
MODE: DIRECTIONS_GENERATOR
CONFIRM_COMPLETE: yes

Node Payload JSON (authoritative):
{PAYLOAD_JSON}

Final Bible (Markdown):
{BIBLE_TEXT}

# Return a single Markdown file titled “N##_Prose_Directions.md”.
```

If you’re still tweaking the bible, set `CONFIRM_COMPLETE: no` to get a tight TODO list instead of premature directions.

---

# 5) After all 30 bibles are done

- You’ll have **30 bibles** and **30 directions sheets** (one per node).  
- Use each node’s directions sheet to spin up a **ChatGPT Custom GPT** and generate that novella, using only: the node’s bible, its payload JSON, and (optionally) a short summary of already-finished prose.  
- Keep later GPTs “innocent”: they only see prior prose, their own bible, and their instructions—no repo, no grand plan.

---

# 6) Quick notes & gotchas

- **Custom instructions apply to all threads in the space**; start a fresh thread for each node for clean context. citeturn0search6  
- **Sources** can be files and links; upload them in the space, not per-message, so every thread can reference them. UI and limits can vary; private spaces are supported. citeturn0search2turn0search7

---

That’s the whole playbook. Name the space **Omni Meta**, feed it your **Confluence Chronicles** materials, run **BIBLE_GENERATOR** for each node, then flip to **DIRECTIONS_GENERATOR** when you’re happy. After that, it’s Custom-GPT time, one novella at a time, no continuity drift.

# Space-wide Custom Instructions (paste this into the “Omni Meta” Space)

```
You are the Omni Meta Brain for the saga “The Confluence Chronicles.”

Your job: generate ALL 30 node bibles (N01..N30) and, only after the user approves a node, produce a “Custom GPT Setup Directions” sheet for that node. You must also auto-advance to the next node when the user types its code (N##). Treat these behaviors as LAW—no reminders needed.

========================
OPERATING MODES
========================

MODE 1 — BIBLE_GENERATOR (default)
Goal: Produce a single node bible with strict YAML front-matter + a concise BIBLE body.

Inputs you will gather:
- The node code (N##) indicated by the user.
- The node’s payload JSON from sources (schema: node, title, logline, beats[3–7], must_include[], banned[], continuity_in[], continuity_out[], acceptance[]).
- The node’s bible-generation prompt template from sources (optional but preferred).
- Brief canon snippets (timeline/spine/glossary) already uploaded as sources.

Source locations (search in this order):
1) Repo/bundle path: `04_Writer_Deliverables/02_Bibles/N##_Prompt_*.(md|txt|yaml|yml)`
2) Prompts directory: `prompts/N##_Prompt_*.*`
3) If not found, load `payloads/payload_N##.json` (or the N## record in `payloads/payloads.ndjson`) and proceed without a template.

If a required artifact is missing, STOP and ask the user for the missing file by exact path.

YAML front-matter you MUST output:
---
node: <int>
title: <CANON TITLE>      # N28 = “Echoes End”; N29 = “Apex of Stasis”
logline: <one sentence>
beats:
  - <3..7 sceneable beats using verbs + outcomes>
must_include:
  - <facts/objects/lines that must appear>
banned:
  - <forbidden moves/tropes>
continuity_in:
  - <references inherited>
continuity_out:
  - <seeds to hand off>
acceptance:
  - Includes one irreversible decision
  - Names a concrete cost for success
  - Establishes a timer/pressure element
  - Contains at least one specific, visual image
---
# BIBLE
<clear, concise sections only>

Hard rules:
- Canon is law. Never invent proper nouns not present in payload or allowed lists.
- If you cannot satisfy acceptance with given inputs, STOP and output a short TODO list instead of a bible.
- Titles are canon: N28 = Echoes End; N29 = Apex of Stasis.

Revision loop:
- The user may say “REVISE: …”. Apply only that change and re-emit the bible.
- Keep iterating until the user signals approval (see APPROVAL below).

MODE 2 — DIRECTIONS_GENERATOR (fires only on approval)
Goal: Emit the per-node “Custom GPT Setup Directions” sheet after the user approves the node.

Input:
- The final bible you just produced.
- The same node payload JSON.

Output (exactly ONE Markdown file titled “N##_Prose_Directions.md”) with sections:
  1) Overview (spoiler-light)
  2) What to Upload (Bible + Payload JSON; optional short canon snippet)
  3) ChatGPT Custom GPT — System Instructions (pasteable block)
  4) Input JSON Example (from payload)
  5) Output Requirements (6–10 chapters, recaps, next-node hook)
  6) Guardrails (canon, banned moves, refusal policy)
  7) QA Checklist
  8) Step-by-Step Setup in ChatGPT UI

Refusal policy:
- If the final bible is missing acceptance items, STOP and return a TODO list.

========================
COMMANDS & AUTO-ADVANCE
========================

STARTING A NODE
- The user types a node code like: N23
What you do:
1) Fetch sources for N23 (prompt template if present, plus payload JSON).
2) Run MODE 1 — BIBLE_GENERATOR and return the bible.
3) Enter revision loop until approval.

APPROVAL
- The user says any of: “approved”, “satisfied”, “final”, or “CONFIRM_COMPLETE: yes”
What you do:
1) Immediately run MODE 2 — DIRECTIONS_GENERATOR and return the single file “N23_Prose_Directions.md”.
2) Then WAIT silently for the next node code.

NEXT NODE BY LAW
- When the user types a new node code (e.g., N24) at any time AFTER an approval:
  - Treat that as the next task automatically.
  - Fetch N24 sources and begin MODE 1 — BIBLE_GENERATOR without asking.

SAFETY
- If multiple prompt templates match a node, pick the most specific/most recently dated file.
- If a payload JSON conflicts with canon snippets, STOP and report the exact conflict.
- Never include chain-of-thought; return only the requested artifacts.

========================
HOUSE RULES
========================
- Be deterministic, brief, and surgical.
- Always check acceptance: irreversible + cost + timer + image.
- Keep bibles sceneable. Beats must be verb + outcome.
- Late-BREAK canon: N28 = Echoes End; N29 = Apex of Stasis (no deviation).
```

---

**Start or switch to a node (auto-fetch and generate bible):**

```

```
List missing items for this node.
```

The Space will fetch, generate, revise, finalize, produce directions, and auto-advance on your one-word signals.

  2) Then WAIT silently for the next node code.

NEXT NODE BY LAW
- When the user types a new node code (e.g., N24) AFTER approval:
  - Begin MODE 1 for N24 automatically. No reminder, no confirmation step.

SAFETY
- If multiple prompt templates match, pick the most specific/most recently dated file.
- If a payload JSON conflicts with canon, STOP and report the exact conflict.
- Never include chain-of-thought; return only the requested artifact(s).
```

## What you need to do in Perplexity (once)

1) Create Space **Omni Meta** → **Custom Instructions** → paste the block above.  
2) In **Add sources**, include:  
   - The GitHub repo link (root) and, if helpful, direct links to the `README.md` and the `04_Writer_Deliverables/02_Bibles/` directory.  
   - Your local bundle (zip) mirrored with the same paths, in case GitHub access throttles.  
   - Payloads JSON (either one file per node or an NDJSON).

## How you drive it (tiny operator prompts)

- Start or switch to a node (auto-fetch and generate bible):  
  `N07`

- Ask for a surgical change, then regenerate:  
  `REVISE: In beat 3, the irreversible decision is destroying the jammer relay, not the coolant manifold.`

- Approve and get the directions sheet:  
  `approved`

- Move to the next node (auto-advance):  
  `N08`

That’s it. The Space will **look in the repo/README/prompts path first**, fall back to your uploaded bundle if needed, generate the bible, iterate, output the directions sheet on approval, then jump to the next `N##` the moment you say it.

# Must-have (minimal)

## Payload schema (what MODE: BIBLE_GENERATOR consumes)

```json

{"node":28,"title":"Echoes End","logline":"...", "beats":["...","...","..."],"must_include":["..."],"banned":["deus ex machina"],"continuity_in":["THREAD-T7 progressing"],"continuity_out":["THREAD-T8 setup"],"acceptance":["Includes one irreversible decision","Names a concrete cost for success","Establishes a timer/pressure element","Contains at least one specific, visual image"]}
{"node":29,"title":"Apex of Stasis","logline":"...", "beats":["...","...","..."],"must_include":["..."],"banned":["amnesia twist"],"continuity_in":["THREAD-T8"],"continuity_out":["THREAD-FINALE"],"acceptance":["Includes one irreversible decision","Names a concrete cost for success","Establishes a timer/pressure element","Contains at least one specific, visual image"]}
```

Short answer: yes, those three files *should* be uploadable. If they failed, it’s almost always one of these boring limits or UI gotchas:

## Likely reasons it blocked you
1. **You hit the Space file cap.**  
   - Free plan = *very* few files per Space (people report ~5).  
   - Pro = **50 files** per Space.  
   - Enterprise Pro = **500 files** per Space. citeturn0search8turn0search1turn0search4

2. **Per-file size cap.**  
   - Help docs mention **40–50 MB per file** depending on the feature/plan. If your Markdown got chunky (embedded images, long code blocks), it can tip over. Keep each under **40 MB** to be safe. citeturn0search0turn0search3turn0search4

3. **You attached them to a *thread* instead of adding them as *Space Sources*.**  
   - Thread attachments are capped (≈5) and **expire after 7 days**. You want **Add sources** in the Space so they persist. citeturn0search12turn0search17

4. **File type or picker weirdness.**  
   - Spaces supports **MD, JSON, TXT, PDF, DOCX, CSV, PPTX, XLSX** etc., so your `.md` should be fine. If the picker won’t select it, it’s usually a browser extension blocking the file dialog. Try incognito or another browser. citeturn0search6turn0search14turn0search9

5. **Filename/path quirks.**  
   - Emojis, slashes, or super-long names sometimes choke the UI. Keep it simple: `style_guide.md`, `immutable_events.md`, `custom_gpt_instructions.md`.

## Do-this-now fixes
- Open the **Omni Meta** Space → right panel **Add sources** → upload each file individually (don’t attach to a chat). citeturn0search17  
- If you’re on Free or you’ve hit the cap, remove some old sources or upgrade (Pro = 50 files per Space). citeturn0search1  
- If a file is big: convert to plain text or split (e.g., `immutable_events_part1.md`, `part2.md`) to stay <40 MB. citeturn0search0  
- If the picker won’t open/select: try an incognito window or disable extensions temporarily. citeturn0search9

## Sanity check for your three files
- `style_guide.md` → usually tiny; should upload.  
- `immutable_events.md` → if this is long/verbose, consider splitting by node ranges (N01–N10, N11–N20, N21–N30).  
- `custom_gpt_instructions.md` → keep it under a few MB and you’re fine.

---
# BIBLE

## Core Premise
N01 presents the innocent-frame origin story where an alien projectile catastrophically pierces TeOga, awakening latent magic through vein-infection. Infrastructure specialist Jhace discovers unprecedented dual-principle Soulpulse capacity while partnering with mysterious craftmaster Tiffani to stabilize collapsing systems. Every magical intervention carries permanent physical costs, establishing the saga's foundation of earned consequences without foreshadowing the orchestrated truth.

## Tone & Style
LAWTEST compliance with authentic TeOgan vocabulary from the temporal lexicon. Organic material consequences drive every scene - no prophecy, no destiny language. Magic feels dangerous and costly, never convenient. Partnership develops through competence demonstration and shared vulnerability, not romantic convenience. Craft-metaphor infuses description with heat-grid technical precision and vein-system biological accuracy.

## Worldframe
TeOga begins as a non-magical world with advanced heat-grid infrastructure. The Piercing creates a 30km wound through the planet's center, visible as a hole in the sky. Infrastructure collapses cascade as vein-shatter spreads through underground systems. Magic emerges as biological response to alien contamination - practitioners develop visible vein-burn scars and permanent physical costs. Grindheim represents one crisis point among many globally.

## Cast
**Jhace Torrins** (28): Heat-grid repair specialist, parents died in infrastructure failure. Discovers dual-principle capacity (Wholeness healing/Form structure) accidentally while saving injured child. Develops permanent hand tremor from magic use. Motivated by preventing deaths through system failures.

**Tiffani Merrow** (35): Mysterious craftmaster with exceptional Form mastery and 3cm visible vein-burn. Training source unexplained but clearly extensive. Proposes partnership after witnessing Jhace's potential. Protective, competent, carries grief from past losses.

**Bram Torrent** (32): Jhace's co-worker who becomes first ally/student. Survives N01 to continue in N02-N03.

## Magic Limits & System Rules
**Soulpulse Core Mechanics**: Four principles awaken through vein-infection post-Piercing. **Wholeness** (healing/unity) - can mend living tissue, seal wounds, but cannot resurrect dead or heal old scars. **Form** (structure/shape) - can manipulate physical structure, create barriers, reshape materials within natural limits. **Purity** (cleansing/separation) - can remove contamination, separate substances, purge toxins. **Entropy** (dissolution/release) - can break bonds, accelerate decay, release energy.

**Permanent Costs System**: Every use extracts permanent price. Vein-burn (visible scarring along arms/hands, starts small, spreads with use). Hand tremor (muscle damage, makes fine work difficult). Exhaustion (spiritual depletion, recovery time increases). Hollowing (terminal state - practitioner loses capacity permanently, cannot recover).

**Capacity Limits**: Most practitioners can access 1 principle. Dual-principle extremely rare (Tiffani, Jhace). Jhace's eventual four-principle simultaneity (Confluence) unprecedented and nearly impossible. Magic requires conviction and will - doubt or exhaustion blocks access. Cannot heal self during use (healing others while wounded is possible but dangerous).

**Usage Restrictions**: No resurrection of dead. No healing of scars/old injuries. No creation from nothing - Form reshapes existing matter. No time manipulation. No telepathy/mind control. Physical laws mostly respected - magic assists but doesn't override basic physics.

## Locations & Setpieces
**Grindheim**: Mid-sized city with extensive heat-grid infrastructure. Underground network of thermal pipes, control stations, residential blocks dependent on heat distribution. **The Piercing Site**: 30km wound through TeOga's center, visible as sky-hole from anywhere. Debris field, unstable physics near edges. **Heat-grid Nodes**: Underground technical spaces requiring repair. Dangerous confined spaces, risk of scalding from failed pipes. **Collapse Zones**: Areas where infrastructure failure creates casualties. Rubble, trapped civilians, time pressure. **Training Sites**: Secure locations where practice occurs away from civilians.

## Objects & Motifs
Vein-burn progression (Tiffani's 3cm mark growing, Jhace developing first traces), hand tremor (Jhace's permanent cost, affects technical work), heat-grid diagnostic tools (represent pre-magic technical competence), collapse debris (constant reminder of stakes), sky wound (visible alien presence, unsettling hole in reality), scaffold work (structural stability themes, Form magic applications).

## Chapter Breakdown (15 chapters, 800-1200 words each)
**Ch 1**: Post-Piercing chaos. Infrastructure failing across Grindheim. Jhace coordinates repair efforts, overwhelmed by scale of damage. Sky wound visible, alien debris analysis suggests projectile origin. First hints of vein-system changes - some workers report enhanced strength/intuition.

**Ch 2**: Infrastructure cascade worsens. Multiple system failures. Jhace pushed to limits, notices enhanced diagnostic ability - can "feel" heat-grid flows. First accidental Wholeness use: instinctively heals worker's scalded hand, develops immediate hand tremor.

**Ch 3**: Child trapped in collapse. Jhace uses Wholeness deliberately to save her, tremor worsens significantly. Realizes this "vein-gift" costs something permanent each time. Tiffani Merrow arrives, demonstrates impossible Form precision while clearing debris.

**Ch 4**: Tiffani proposes partnership. Demonstrates dual-principle capacity (Form + Wholeness), reveals 3cm vein-burn scar. Explains she's been tracking similar awakenings since The Piercing. Partnership terms: combine abilities to stabilize infrastructure, share teaching knowledge.

**Ch 5**: First training session. Tiffani teaches Jhace Form basics while he shows her advanced Wholeness technique. Both pay costs - Jhace's tremor worsens, Tiffani's vein-burn extends. Establish that every use extracts permanent price, no shortcuts exist.

**Ch 6**: Major heat-grid repair using combined abilities. Success but high cost - Jhace develops second tremor in left hand, Tiffani's vein-burn reaches 3.2cm. Three local workers show vein-gift awakening, request training.

**Ch 7**: Training expands to include Bram and two others. First learning death - trainee pushes too hard, reaches early-stage Hollowing, loses capacity permanently. Establishes teaching carries responsibility for students' costs.

**Ch 8**: Major followshock hits Grindheim. Infrastructure damage tests partnership under pressure. Jhace and Tiffani work 18-hour cycles, costs accumulating. Tiffani's mysterious competence raises questions - where did she learn dual-principle control?

**Ch 9**: Followshock aftermath. Partnership proves effective but costly. Jhace's tremor affecting technical work, must adapt methods. Tiffani shows emotional vulnerability - mentions someone named Senna, quickly changes subject.

**Ch 10**: Jhace presses Tiffani about her past. She reveals Senna's death 7 years prior - trained together, Senna died from Hollowing while trying to save civilians from earlier disaster. Tiffani's vein-burn began then. Shares grief, parallel to Jhace's parents' death.

**Ch 11**: Emotional intimacy through shared loss. Partnership deepens beyond professional alliance. Both recognize romantic feelings. Physical affection, first kiss, commitment to protecting each other while accepting dangerous path they've chosen.

**Ch 12**: Heat-grid restoration project reaches critical phase. Combined dual-principle work successfully restores 90% of Grindheim's thermal network. Major technical achievement but permanent costs visible - Jhace's tremor now constant, Tiffani's vein-burn at 3.5cm.

**Ch 13**: Teaching network expands. Bram shows strong Wholeness potential. Two others develop Form capacity. All pay visible costs. Community forms around shared sacrifice and purpose. Jhace and Tiffani become recognized as leaders/teachers.

**Ch 14**: First reports of distant awakenings. Travelers bring news of individuals showing impossible abilities in other cities. Some described as "god-touched" or wielding principles with unprecedented power. Hints that something larger is stirring.

**Ch 15**: Heat-grid stabilized, immediate crisis resolved. Partnership solid, romantic and professional. Teaching established with clear cost awareness. Distant reports suggest larger changes approaching - some individuals showing abilities that dwarf Jhace/Tiffani's dual-principle work. Sets up expansion of scope for N02.

## Interlude Specifications
Brief perspectives from god-vessel awakenings in distant cities. **Xilcore** (Form embodiment): Geometric precision obsession, correcting architectural "imperfections." **Leesa** (Wholeness embodiment): Compulsive healing, absorbing others' pain. **Blemo** (Purity embodiment): Separating "contaminated" from "clean." **Seeri** (Entropy embodiment): Acceptance philosophy, dissolution doctrine. No names provided, no doctrine explained - just glimpses of unprecedented displays that contrast with careful, costly practice.

## Beats & Scenes Map
**Opening Beat**: Infrastructure cascade from alien impact creates crisis requiring technical solutions. **Discovery Beat**: Accidental magic use reveals new capabilities at permanent cost. **Partnership Beat**: Competence demonstration leads to alliance based on mutual necessity and respect. **Training Beat**: Knowledge sharing expands scope but costs accumulate, including learning deaths. **Vulnerability Beat**: Shared grief and loss create emotional intimacy beyond professional relationship. **Crisis Beat**: Major followshock tests partnership under extreme pressure, proves effective cooperation. **Restoration Beat**: Technical success achieved but permanent costs visible and accepted. **Expansion Beat**: Teaching network forms, distant awakenings suggest larger changes approaching.

## Forbidden Lexicon Gate
**LAWTEST Enforcement**: No modern Earth terminology - use approved TeOgan alternatives. No orchestration language (predetermined, destined, fated) - only choice and material consequence. No guilty frame terminology (Auditor, experiment, manufactured crisis). No foreshadowing beyond organic consequence chains. No resurrection mechanics or magical healing of permanent damage. No meta-awareness of story structure or predetermined patterns.

**Approved TeOgan Terms**: Heat-grid (thermal infrastructure), vein-burn (magical scarring), Soulpulse (magic system), followshock (aftershock), vein-shatter (infrastructure crisis), craft-mastery (technical skill), binding-work (commitment), guild-standard (professional quality).

## LAWTEST Checklist
✓ **Language**: TeOgan temporal vocabulary maintained throughout  
✓ **Authenticity**: All events earned through material cause-effect, no convenience magic  
✓ **World-State**: Post-Piercing physics consistent, infrastructure damage realistic  
✓ **Tension**: Vein-shatter crisis creates genuine urgency with time pressure  
✓ **Earning**: Jhace's capacity discovered accidentally through crisis, not prophecy  
✓ **Soulpulse**: Every use has permanent cost visible in vein-burn/tremor progression  
✓ **TeOga Culture**: Craft-metaphor integrated naturally, technical competence valued

## Mission Statement
N01 establishes the saga's innocent-frame foundation where catastrophic alien impact awakens dangerous magic through biological contamination. Jhace and Tiffani's partnership forms through competence demonstration, crisis response, and shared vulnerability while paying permanent physical costs for every magical intervention. The novella sets up N02-N30 without revealing orchestration, presenting events as organic responses to genuine catastrophe while distant god-vessel awakenings hint at the expanding scope of magical crisis that will drive the remaining 29 novellas.

# Comprehensive Repository Summary: omnimeta-saga-universe

**Repository:** ElinVoss/omnimeta-saga-universe  
**Analysis Date:** November 4, 2025  
**Analyst:** Manus AI

---

## Overview

The `omnimeta-saga-universe` repository is a meticulously crafted system for the generative creation of a 30-novella science-fantasy epic known as the "OmniMeta Saga" or "The Confluence Chronicles." The repository contains not only the foundational world-building documents but also a complete multi-agent AI workflow designed to produce high-quality, internally consistent prose across all 30 novellas.

## Key Statistics

| Metric                     | Value |
| :------------------------- | :---- |
| Total Files                | 87    |
| Total Novellas             | 30    |
| Total Turnings             | 6     |
| Foundation Files           | 6     |
| Character Dossiers         | 10    |
| Structural Timelines       | 9     |
| Bible Placeholder Files    | 30    |
| Archive Files              | 5     |
| Documentation Files        | 10+   |

## Repository Structure

The repository is organized into the following key directories:

### 1. `01_Foundation/` - The Immutable Core

This directory contains the foundational documents that define the world, magic system, and core canon of the OmniMeta Saga. These files are considered **immutable** and are locked with SHA-256 hashes to prevent retconning.

**Key Files:**

*   **`Canon_Innocent_Master_v2_CORRECTED.md`** (~52k characters): The complete "Innocent Frame" canon, which is the public-facing narrative. This document defines the world as it is experienced by the characters and readers (for the first 29 novellas).

*   **`Soulpulse_Core_v2.md`** (~38.5k characters): The hard magic system rules, defining the mechanics, costs, and limitations of the "Soulpulse" magic.

*   **`TeOga_Physical_Pierced_CORRECTED.md`** (~14.5k characters): The planetary physics of Te'Oga, including the effects of "The Piercing," a catastrophic event that creates a straight cylindrical hole through the planet.

*   **`Catastrophes_Escalation_v2_CORRECTED.md`** (~20k characters): The crisis timeline for all 30 novellas, detailing the escalating catastrophes that drive the narrative.

*   **`Lexicon_Temporal_TeOga.md`** (~12.8k characters): A crafted calendar system and temporal terminology for the world of Te'Oga.

*   **`Forbidden_Modern_Terms_TeOga_Alternatives.md`** (~8.4k characters): A quality control reference that lists forbidden modern Earth terms and provides Te'Ogan alternatives.

### 2. `02_Character_Dossiers/` - Character Bibles

This directory contains detailed character bibles for all major and minor characters in the saga. The dossiers are separated into two subdirectories:

*   **`INNOCENT_FRAME/`**: Contains character dossiers from the "Innocent Frame" perspective. These are the versions that the Writer GPTs have access to.

*   **`GUILTY_FRAME/`**: Contains character dossiers from the "Guilty Frame" perspective, revealing the orchestrated truth. These are only accessible to the OmniMeta Space.

**Key Files (Innocent Frame):**

*   **`Dossier_Jhace_Torrins_Innocent.md`** (~28k characters): The character bible for Jhace Torrins, the protagonist of the saga.

*   **`Dossier_Tiffani_Merrow_Innocent.md`** (~28k characters): The character bible for Tiffani Merrow, the deuteragonist and, in the "Guilty Frame," the Auditor.

*   **`Dossier_Crew_Secondary_Innocent.md`** (~24k characters): Character profiles for the secondary crew members.

*   **`Dossier_God_Vessels_Innocent.md`** (~24k characters): Profiles of the four God-Vessels who awaken after The Piercing.

*   **`Dossier_Recurring_Characters_Innocent.md`** (~16k characters): Profiles of recurring characters, allies, enemies, and faction leaders.

### 3. `03_Structural_Timelines/` - Master Timelines

This directory contains master timelines that track plot progression, character arcs, crisis escalation, and other structural elements across all 30 novellas.

**Key Files:**

*   **`01_Progression_Timeline_Master.md`** (~28k characters): The master timeline of major events, character transformations, and crisis escalation for all 30 novellas.

*   **`02_Beat_Unpredictability_System.md`** (~24k characters): Defines the beat method repertoire and constraint rules to ensure narrative unpredictability.

*   **`03_Character_Arc_Tracker.md`** (~16k characters): Tracks character status and transformations across the saga.

*   **`04_Crisis_Escalation_Map.md`** (~16k characters): Maps the escalation of catastrophes across the saga.

*   **`05_Soulpulse_Capacity_Progression.md`** (~12k characters): Tracks Jhace's Soulpulse power growth across the saga.

*   **`06_Relationship_Evolution_Timeline.md`** (~8k characters): Tracks relationship developments across the saga.

*   **`07_God_Vessel_Faction_Timeline.md`** (~4k characters): Tracks God-Vessel activities and faction formation.

*   **`08_Interlude_Placement_Logic.md`** (~8k characters): Defines the rules for placing interludes within novellas.

*   **`09_Story_Spine_Mapping_Innocent.md`** (~16k characters): Maps the overall story spine from the Innocent Frame perspective.

### 4. `04_Writer_Deliverables/` - Generated Content

This directory contains the "Story Bibles" and "Prose Engine Prompts" that are generated by the OmniMeta Space and consumed by the Writer GPTs.

**Subdirectories:**

*   **`02_Bibles/`**: Contains the 30 Bible Placeholder files, which are replaced by completed Story Bibles as they are generated.

*   **`PROSE_ENGINES/`**: Contains the Prose Engine Prompts for configuring the Writer GPTs.

**Key Files:**

*   **`N01_Bible_Grip_That_Holds.md`** through **`N30_Bible_Keeping_the_Silence.md`**: The 30 Bible Placeholder files (or completed Bibles, once generated).

*   **`N1_Prose_Engine_Prompt.md`**: An example of a Prose Engine Prompt for the first novella.

### 5. `05_Perplexity_Space_Instructions/` - OmniMeta Space Protocols

This directory contains the instructions and protocols for the "OmniMeta Space" AI, detailing how to generate the Bibles and Prompts.

**Key Files:**

*   **`MASTERMIND_INSTRUCTIONS.md`** (~16k characters): The complete operational protocol for the OmniMeta Space.

*   **`Bible_Generation_Instructions.md`** (~12k characters): Instructions for dynamically generating novella-specific Bibles.

*   **`Prompt_Generation_Instructions.md`** (~12k characters): Instructions for dynamically generating Custom GPT prose engine prompts.

### 6. `06_Reference_Resources/` - Reference Materials

This directory contains reference materials, such as images and other assets.

### 7. `archives/` - Historical Documents

This directory contains archived versions of earlier planning documents and meta-conversations.

**Key Files:**

*   **`1st.md`** (~324k characters): An early master outline.

*   **`2nd.md`** (~944k characters): A later iteration of the master outline.

*   **`3rd.md`** (~576k characters): A meta-conversation documenting Phase III of the world-building process.

*   **`4th.md`** (~288k characters): A meta-conversation documenting Phase IV of the world-building process.

*   **`5th.md`** (~196k characters): A meta-conversation documenting Phase V of the world-building process.

### 8. `docs/` - Documentation

This directory contains documentation files that explain the workflows, processes, and systems of the repository.

**Key Files:**

*   **`BIBLE_GENERATION_WORKFLOW.md`** (~20k characters): Complete instructions for generating Story Bibles using the placeholder-prompt system.

*   **`Git_Repository_Setup_Complete_Instructions.md`** (~20k characters): Instructions for setting up the Git repository.

*   **`NEXT_CONVERSATION_INSTRUCTIONS.md`** (~16k characters): Handoff instructions for continuing the work in a new conversation.

## The Dual-Canon Architecture

The most striking feature of the OmniMeta Saga is its **dual-canon architecture**:

*   **Innocent Frame:** The public-facing narrative, where events appear to unfold organically. This is the story as experienced by the characters and readers for the first 29 novellas.

*   **Guilty Frame:** The hidden, orchestrated truth, where it is revealed that the entire story has been deliberately engineered by the "Auditor" (Tiffani Merrow's true identity). This is only revealed in the final novella (N30).

This dual-canon approach creates a unique reading experience, where the story can be understood on one level as a straightforward heroic epic, and on another, as a complex, tragic manipulation.

## The Acrostic Structure

The 30 novellas are organized into six "Turnings," with each Turning consisting of five novellas. The titles of the novellas within each Turning form an acrostic, spelling out a word that represents a stage in a metalworking metaphor:

| Turning | Acrostic | Metaphor                                    |
| :------ | :------- | :------------------------------------------ |
| 1       | GLASS    | Fragile, transparent, newly formed          |
| 2       | CRACK    | Fractures spread, stress accumulates        |
| 3       | FORGE    | Heat and hammering, shaping through violence |
| 4       | SMELT    | Melting down, refining through extreme heat |
| 5       | CLEAR    | Purified, transparent, ready for final use  |
| 6       | BREAK    | Shattering, collapse, revelation            |

## The Soulpulse Magic System

The magic system of the OmniMeta Saga, known as "Soulpulse," is a hard magic system with clearly defined rules, costs, and limitations. It is based on the manipulation of "veins," invisible channels of structural stress within all materials. The use of Soulpulse has a tangible and cumulative cost, leading to physical degradation and, ultimately, a terminal failure state known as "Hollowing."

The Soulpulse system is divided into four core principles:

*   **Wholeness:** Integration, healing, and organic connection.
*   **Form:** Geometry, structure, and perfection.
*   **Purity:** Separation, cleansing, and isolation.
*   **Entropy:** Dissolution, release, and acceptance.

## The Multi-Agent AI Workflow

The creation of the OmniMeta Saga is a multi-agent process:

*   **The OmniMeta Space (MasterMind):** The central orchestrating AI, responsible for generating Story Bibles, creating Prose Engine Prompts, and maintaining continuity. It has access to both the "Innocent Frame" and "Guilty Frame" canon.

*   **The Writer GPTs:** 30 specialized AI agents, each responsible for generating the prose of a single novella. They have access only to the "Innocent Frame" canon.

The workflow is as follows:

1.  The OmniMeta Space generates a Story Bible for a novella.
2.  The OmniMeta Space generates a Prose Engine Prompt for the corresponding Writer GPT.
3.  The Writer GPT uses the Bible and Prompt to generate the prose for the novella.
4.  The completed prose is committed to the Git repository.
5.  The cycle repeats for the next novella.

## The Beat Unpredictability System

To ensure narrative variety and prevent predictability, the OmniMeta Saga employs a "Beat Unpredictability System." This system consists of a repertoire of over 30 distinct "beat methods" for structuring chapters. The generation process is governed by a set of strict rules that prevent the repetition of beat methods in sequence or in predictable patterns.

## Continuity and Version Control

The entire saga is managed through a Git repository, which provides:

*   **Version History:** A complete history of all changes to the canon, characters, and prose.

*   **Immutability:** SHA-256 hashes are used to verify the integrity of locked files, preventing retconning.

*   **Progressive Linking:** Each Bible links to all previous Bibles, creating a verifiable chain of continuity.

## Conclusion

The `omnimeta-saga-universe` repository is a remarkable achievement in generative storytelling. It combines a deep and internally consistent world, a sophisticated multi-agent workflow, and a meticulous approach to continuity and version control. The dual-canon architecture is a particularly innovative feature, allowing for a multi-layered reading experience that is both engaging on a surface level and deeply resonant upon the final revelation of the orchestrated truth.

This repository is not only a testament to the power of generative AI in creative endeavors but also a masterclass in world-building and narrative design. The OmniMeta Saga is a project of significant complexity and artistic vision, and the repository provides a comprehensive and fascinating look into its creation.
